I want to build a learn basic English for my Thai wife but it will have to be from the beginning sounding pronunciation sylibuls small common words with their meaning and it will have to have voice to voice

## Response:
07/04/2026, 20:25:14

I can outline it now and base it on a beginner-first structure. Unless you want a mobile app spec, I’ll assume you want a practical course/app plan with Thai support, pronunciation, syllable practice, and speaking/listening features.

> Thought for 10s

Yes. What you need is a **very beginner English program for a Thai speaker**, built in this order:

1.  **sound first**
2.  **syllables next**
3.  **small common words**
4.  **short useful sentences**
5.  **voice listening**
6.  **voice speaking back**
7.  **slow repetition every day**

A good design is **not grammar first**. It should be **ears, mouth, then words**.

Best structure
--------------

### Phase 1: English sounds

Start with the sounds that are hard for Thai learners.

Teach:

*   a / e / i / o / u
*   b / p
*   t / d
*   k / g
*   s / z
*   sh / ch
*   l / r
*   th
*   v / w
*   final consonants

For each sound:

*   hear the sound
*   see mouth position
*   repeat slowly
*   compare two similar sounds

Example:

*   **rice** / **lice**
*   **right** / **light**
*   **very** / **wary**
*   **thin** / **tin**

This part needs:

*   audio playback
*   slow playback
*   microphone recording
*   compare her voice to model voice

Phase 2: syllables
------------------

Use very small sound blocks first.

Examples:

*   ba, be, bi, bo, bu
*   pa, pe, pi, po, pu
*   ma, me, mi, mo, mu
*   ta, da, ka, ga
*   sa, sha, cha
*   la, ra
*   wa, va

Then move to one-syllable words:

*   cat
*   dog
*   book
*   pen
*   cup
*   bag
*   rice
*   milk
*   go
*   stop
*   yes
*   no

Then two-syllable words:

*   water
*   happy
*   baby
*   table
*   open
*   teacher
*   morning

Phase 3: first 100 common words
-------------------------------

Do not teach random dictionary words. Teach **survival words** first.

### Group 1: people

*   I
*   you
*   he
*   she
*   we
*   they
*   mother
*   father
*   husband
*   wife
*   baby
*   friend

### Group 2: daily actions

*   go
*   come
*   eat
*   drink
*   sleep
*   sit
*   stand
*   look
*   listen
*   speak
*   want
*   need
*   like
*   help

### Group 3: home words

*   house
*   room
*   bed
*   door
*   chair
*   table
*   spoon
*   cup
*   rice
*   water
*   food

### Group 4: useful adjectives

*   big
*   small
*   hot
*   cold
*   good
*   bad
*   happy
*   sad
*   open
*   closed
*   new
*   old

### Group 5: question words

*   what
*   where
*   who
*   when
*   why
*   how

Each word screen should show:

*   the English word
*   simple meaning in Thai
*   audio
*   syllable split
*   slow pronunciation
*   example sentence
*   record-and-repeat

Example:

**Water**

*   Meaning: น้ำ
*   Syllables: wa-ter
*   Pronunciation: /WAW-ter/
*   Example: “I want water.”

Phase 4: sentence patterns
--------------------------

Teach sentence frames, not isolated grammar rules.

Start with:

*   I am \_\_\_.
*   You are \_\_\_.
*   This is \_\_\_.
*   I want \_\_\_.
*   I like \_\_\_.
*   I need \_\_\_.
*   Where is \_\_\_?
*   Can you help me?
*   Please.
*   Thank you.
*   I don’t understand.

Examples:

*   I am tired.
*   I want rice.
*   I need water.
*   This is my bag.
*   Where is the bathroom?
*   Please help me.

Phase 5: voice-to-voice
-----------------------

This is important for her.

The app should have **two voice modes**:

### Mode 1: Listen and repeat

*   app says: “Hello”
*   she repeats: “Hello”
*   app checks pronunciation
*   app gives simple feedback:
    *   good
    *   try again
    *   say it slower
    *   stress first syllable

### Mode 2: simple conversation

The app speaks and waits for reply.

Example:

*   App: “What is your name?”
*   User: “My name is Mali.”
*   App: “Nice to meet you.”
*   User: “Nice to meet you too.”

Later:

*   App: “What do you want to eat?”
*   User: “I want rice.”
*   App: “Do you want water?”
*   User: “Yes, please.”

What features it should have
----------------------------

For a first version, include these:

### Core features

*   Thai interface
*   English audio by native speaker
*   slow audio button
*   syllable breakdown
*   microphone recording
*   speech recognition
*   pronunciation score
*   repeat difficult words
*   spaced repetition
*   daily lesson 10 to 15 minutes
*   picture support
*   simple quizzes

### Important extra features

*   compare similar sounds
*   mouth-shape animation
*   male and female voice options
*   offline audio download
*   “speak with husband” practice mode

Best lesson format
------------------

Each lesson should be very short.

### Lesson template

1.  1 new sound
2.  5 syllables
3.  5 words
4.  2 sentences
5.  listen and repeat
6.  mini conversation
7.  review

Example:

### Lesson 1

Sound:

*   b

Syllables:

*   ba, be, bi, bo, bu

Words:

*   book
*   bag
*   baby
*   bed
*   big

Sentences:

*   This is a book.
*   My bag is big.

Conversation:

*   App: “What is this?”
*   User: “It is a book.”

First 4 weeks plan
------------------

### Week 1

*   alphabet sounds
*   vowels
*   easy one-syllable words
*   yes/no
*   hello/goodbye/thank you

### Week 2

*   common objects
*   food and drink
*   I want / I like / I need

### Week 3

*   people and family
*   numbers
*   time basics
*   where is / this is

### Week 4

*   home conversation
*   shopping basics
*   restaurant basics
*   simple question and answer speaking

Important design rule for Thai learners
---------------------------------------

Thai speakers often need extra work on:

*   final consonants
*   consonant clusters
*   r/l distinction
*   v/w distinction
*   th sound
*   word stress
*   sentence rhythm

So do not teach only spelling. Teach:

*   **hear it**
*   **see it**
*   **say it**
*   **compare it**
*   **use it in a sentence**

Simple content example
----------------------

### Word card

**Rice**  
Meaning: ข้าว  
Syllables: rice  
Sound: /raɪs/  
Example: “I eat rice.”  
Thai help: ฉันกินข้าว

### Word card

**Water**  
Meaning: น้ำ  
Syllables: wa-ter  
Example: “I want water.”  
Thai help: ฉันต้องการน้ำ

### Word card

**Help**  
Meaning: ช่วย  
Syllables: help  
Example: “Please help me.”  
Thai help: กรุณาช่วยฉัน

If you want to build it as an app
---------------------------------

A clean app structure would be:

*   **Home**
*   **Today’s Lesson**
*   **Sounds**
*   **Words**
*   **Sentences**
*   **Speak Practice**
*   **Review**
*   **Progress**

Best tech direction
-------------------

If you mean software, the simplest build is:

*   **Frontend:** Flutter or React Native
*   **Backend:** Firebase or Supabase
*   **Text-to-speech:** English voice engine
*   **Speech-to-text:** speech recognition API
*   **Pronunciation scoring:** speech assessment API
*   **Audio storage:** cloud storage
*   **Curriculum data:** JSON or database

My recommendation
-----------------

Do this in 3 layers:

**Layer 1: course content**  
Create the sounds, syllables, 100 words, and 200 short sentences.

**Layer 2: voice system**  
Add listen-repeat, record-playback, and pronunciation feedback.

**Layer 3: guided conversation**  
Add beginner voice dialogues for home, food, shopping, travel, and family.

The biggest mistake would be making it too advanced too early.

Start with:

*   20 sounds
*   50 syllables
*   100 words
*   50 sentences
*   20 mini dialogues

That is enough for a strong beginner version.

I can draft the **full beginner curriculum**, or I can turn this into a **complete app specification with screens, features, and database structure**.

## Prompt:
07/04/2026, 20:41:26

full beginner curriculum

## Response:
07/04/2026, 20:41:27

I’m building this as a true zero-beginner sequence for a Thai speaker: sounds, syllables, core words, sentence frames, and speaking practice in the right order. After the curriculum, I’ll also include a lesson pattern you can reuse for every unit.

> Thought for 5s

Below is a **full beginner curriculum** for your Thai wife, designed for **absolute zero English** and built in the correct sequence:

**hear the sound → say the sound → read the syllable → learn the word → say the sentence → do voice practice**

It is designed for:

*   Thai speaker
*   no English background required
*   very small steps
*   pronunciation first
*   common words first
*   voice-to-voice practice included

* * *

Full Beginner English Curriculum
================================

Overall course structure
------------------------

### Level 0: Pre-English foundation

Goal: get comfortable hearing and copying English sounds

### Level 1: Sounds and syllables

Goal: learn basic English pronunciation patterns

### Level 2: First words

Goal: learn very common one-word vocabulary

### Level 3: First sentences

Goal: build tiny daily-use sentences

### Level 4: Basic conversation

Goal: answer and ask simple real-life questions

### Level 5: Daily life English

Goal: use English at home, outside, shopping, food, travel

* * *

Course rules
============

Every lesson should include these 6 parts:

1.  **Listen**
2.  **Repeat**
3.  **Syllables**
4.  **Words**
5.  **Sentence pattern**
6.  **Voice practice**

Keep lessons:

*   10 to 15 minutes
*   only 5 to 10 new words
*   only 1 sentence pattern at a time
*   lots of repetition

* * *

LEVEL 0 — PRE-ENGLISH FOUNDATION
================================

Unit 0.1: Learning how English sounds work
------------------------------------------

Goal:

*   understand that English has different sounds from Thai
*   train listening before speaking

Teach:

*   English has stress
*   English has final consonants
*   English has long and short vowels
*   some English letters have multiple sounds
*   spoken English is not the same as spelling

Practice:

*   listen only
*   repeat only
*   no reading pressure

Examples:

*   cat
*   cap
*   can
*   cup
*   book
*   bed
*   dog
*   big

Voice drills:

*   hear one word
*   repeat one word
*   compare similar words

* * *

Unit 0.2: Mouth and sound awareness
-----------------------------------

Goal:

*   see how mouth shape changes sound

Teach:

*   lips together: b, p, m
*   tongue front: t, d, n, l
*   back mouth: k, g
*   teeth/lip: f, v
*   tongue between teeth: th

Practice minimal pairs:

*   bat / pat
*   fan / van
*   light / right
*   tin / thin
*   west / vest

* * *

LEVEL 1 — SOUNDS AND SYLLABLES
==============================

Module 1A: Vowels
=================

Unit 1: Short vowels
--------------------

Teach:

*   a as in **cat**
*   e as in **bed**
*   i as in **sit**
*   o as in **hot**
*   u as in **cup**

Practice syllables:

*   ba be bi bo bu
*   ma me mi mo mu
*   ta te ti to tu
*   sa se si so su

Words:

*   cat
*   bed
*   sit
*   hot
*   cup

Sentences:

*   It is a cat.
*   This is my cup.

Voice practice:

*   “cat”
*   “bed”
*   “sit”
*   “hot”
*   “cup”

* * *

Unit 2: Long vowels
-------------------

Teach:

*   ee as in **see**
*   ay as in **day**
*   ai as in **my**
*   oa as in **go**
*   oo as in **food**

Words:

*   see
*   day
*   my
*   go
*   food

Sentences:

*   I see you.
*   Let’s go.
*   My food.

Contrast:

*   sit / seat
*   full / fool
*   not / note

* * *

Module 1B: Easy consonants
==========================

Unit 3: B, P, M
---------------

Syllables:

*   ba, pa, ma
*   be, pe, me
*   bi, pi, mi
*   bo, po, mo
*   bu, pu, mu

Words:

*   bag
*   pen
*   map
*   baby
*   mom

Sentences:

*   This is a bag.
*   Mom is here.

Voice drills:

*   bag / back
*   pen / pan
*   baby / maybe

* * *

Unit 4: T, D, N
---------------

Words:

*   tea
*   do
*   ten
*   day
*   nose

Sentences:

*   I do.
*   Ten days.
*   My nose.

Contrast:

*   ten / den
*   do / to

* * *

Unit 5: K, G
------------

Words:

*   cat
*   go
*   come
*   good
*   key

Sentences:

*   Come here.
*   Go now.
*   Good job.

Contrast:

*   coat / goat
*   came / game

* * *

Unit 6: S, Z
------------

Words:

*   see
*   sun
*   zoo
*   zero
*   nose

Sentences:

*   I see the sun.
*   The zoo is big.

Contrast:

*   sip / zip
*   bus / buzz

* * *

Unit 7: F, V
------------

Important for Thai learners.

Words:

*   fan
*   five
*   van
*   very
*   coffee

Sentences:

*   I have five.
*   It is very good.

Contrast:

*   fan / van
*   safe / save

* * *

Unit 8: L, R
------------

Very important.

Words:

*   light
*   rice
*   red
*   long
*   right

Sentences:

*   I like rice.
*   The light is red.
*   Turn right.

Contrast:

*   light / right
*   glass / grass
*   led / red

* * *

Unit 9: W, Y
------------

Words:

*   water
*   we
*   yes
*   you
*   yellow

Sentences:

*   We want water.
*   Yes, thank you.

Contrast:

*   west / vest
*   wine / vine
*   year / ear

* * *

Module 1C: Harder consonants
============================

Unit 10: SH, CH, J
------------------

Words:

*   she
*   shop
*   chair
*   chicken
*   job
*   juice

Sentences:

*   She is in the shop.
*   I want juice.
*   This chair is good.

Contrast:

*   sip / ship
*   cheap / jeep
*   choose / shoes

* * *

Unit 11: TH sounds
------------------

Two kinds:

*   unvoiced: **thin**
*   voiced: **this**

Words:

*   thin
*   thank
*   three
*   this
*   that
*   mother

Sentences:

*   Thank you.
*   This is my mother.
*   That is three.

Contrast:

*   tin / thin
*   day / they
*   dis / this

* * *

Unit 12: NG final sound
-----------------------

Words:

*   sing
*   song
*   long
*   morning
*   thank

Sentences:

*   Good morning.
*   This song is long.

* * *

Module 1D: Final consonants
===========================

Unit 13: Final sounds
---------------------

Very important for Thai learners.

Teach final:

*   p, t, k
*   m, n, ng
*   s, z
*   l, r

Word sets:

*   cap / cat / can
*   back / bag
*   rice / ride
*   help / held
*   pick / pig

Sentences:

*   Pick it up.
*   I need help.
*   This bag is big.

Listening drill:

*   hear the last sound clearly

* * *

Module 1E: Syllable training
============================

Unit 14: One-syllable words
---------------------------

Words:

*   book
*   bag
*   cup
*   rice
*   fish
*   milk
*   dog
*   cat
*   pen
*   phone

Sentence frames:

*   It is a \_\_\_.
*   I want \_\_\_.
*   I like \_\_\_.

* * *

Unit 15: Two-syllable words
---------------------------

Words:

*   water
*   baby
*   happy
*   open
*   table
*   teacher
*   coffee
*   morning
*   noodle
*   chicken

Teach stress:

*   WA-ter
*   TA-ble
*   CHI-cken

Sentences:

*   I want water.
*   The table is big.
*   Good morning.

* * *

Unit 16: Three-syllable introduction
------------------------------------

Words:

*   banana
*   computer
*   family
*   yesterday
*   beautiful

Goal:

*   hear rhythm
*   clap stress

Example:

*   ba-NA-na
*   COM-pu-ter
*   FA-mi-ly

* * *

=====================

Goal:  
build a practical survival vocabulary

LEVEL 3 — FIRST SENTENCES
=========================

Goal:  
build automatic sentence patterns

Teach one pattern at a time.

* * *

Unit 33: “This is \_\_\_.”
--------------------------

Examples:

*   This is a cup.
*   This is my room.
*   This is rice.

Practice:

*   point and say

* * *

Unit 34: “That is \_\_\_.”
--------------------------

Examples:

*   That is my bag.
*   That is the door.
*   That is my husband.

* * *

Unit 35: “It is \_\_\_.”
------------------------

Examples:

*   It is hot.
*   It is cold.
*   It is good.
*   It is big.

* * *

Unit 36: “I am \_\_\_.”
-----------------------

Examples:

*   I am happy.
*   I am tired.
*   I am here.
*   I am ready.

* * *

Unit 37: “You are \_\_\_.”
--------------------------

Examples:

*   You are kind.
*   You are here.
*   You are right.

* * *

Unit 38: “I want \_\_\_.”
-------------------------

Examples:

*   I want water.
*   I want rice.
*   I want coffee.
*   I want help.

* * *

Unit 39: “I need \_\_\_.”
-------------------------

Examples:

*   I need help.
*   I need water.
*   I need a chair.

* * *

Unit 40: “I like \_\_\_.”
-------------------------

Examples:

*   I like tea.
*   I like chicken.
*   I like music.
*   I like English.

* * *

Unit 41: “I don’t want \_\_\_.”
-------------------------------

Examples:

*   I don’t want coffee.
*   I don’t want meat.

* * *

Unit 42: “Can I have \_\_\_?”
-----------------------------

Examples:

*   Can I have water?
*   Can I have a spoon?
*   Can I have rice?

Very useful for daily life.

* * *

Unit 43: “Please” and “Thank you”
---------------------------------

Expressions:

*   Please
*   Thank you
*   Thank you very much
*   You’re welcome

Mini-dialogue:

*   Can I have water?
*   Yes.
*   Thank you.
*   You’re welcome.

* * *

Unit 44: “Where is \_\_\_?”
---------------------------

Examples:

*   Where is the bathroom?
*   Where is my phone?
*   Where is the bag?

* * *

Unit 45: “What is this?”
------------------------

Examples:

*   What is this?
*   It is a spoon.
*   What is that?
*   That is a chair.

* * *

Unit 46: “Who is \_\_\_?”
-------------------------

Examples:

*   Who is he?
*   He is my father.
*   Who is she?
*   She is my friend.

* * *

Unit 47: “Do you want \_\_\_?”
------------------------------

Examples:

*   Do you want rice?
*   Do you want water?
*   Do you want coffee?

Answers:

*   Yes, I do.
*   No, I don’t.

* * *

Unit 48: “Can you help me?”
---------------------------

Examples:

*   Can you help me?
*   Please help me.
*   I need help.

* * *

Unit 49: “I don’t understand.”
------------------------------

Expressions:

*   I don’t understand.
*   Please say it again.
*   Speak slowly, please.
*   What does that mean?

This is essential.

* * *

Unit 50: “I can / I can’t”
--------------------------

Examples:

*   I can read.
*   I can speak a little English.
*   I can’t hear you.
*   I can’t understand.

* * *

LEVEL 4 — BASIC CONVERSATION
============================

Goal:  
use short real-life speaking exchanges

* * *

Module 4A: Greetings
--------------------

Unit 51: Hello and introduction
-------------------------------

Expressions:

*   Hello
*   Hi
*   Good morning
*   Good afternoon
*   Good evening
*   Goodbye
*   See you

Dialogue:

*   Hello.
*   Hello.
*   How are you?
*   I’m fine, thank you.

* * *

Unit 52: Name and identity
--------------------------

Expressions:

*   What is your name?
*   My name is \_\_\_.
*   I am \_\_\_.
*   Nice to meet you.

Dialogue:

*   What is your name?
*   My name is Mali.
*   Nice to meet you.
*   Nice to meet you too.

* * *

Module 4B: Home conversation
----------------------------

Unit 53: At home
----------------

Expressions:

*   Come here.
*   Sit down.
*   Open the door.
*   Close the window.
*   The food is ready.
*   I am in the kitchen.

Dialogue:

*   Where are you?
*   I am in the room.
*   Come here, please.
*   Okay.

* * *

Unit 54: Feelings and needs
---------------------------

Expressions:

*   I am tired.
*   I am hungry.
*   I am thirsty.
*   I am sleepy.
*   I feel sick.

Dialogue:

*   Are you okay?
*   I am tired.
*   Do you want water?
*   Yes, please.

* * *

Module 4C: Food conversation
----------------------------

Unit 55: Meals
--------------

Expressions:

*   I am hungry.
*   I want rice.
*   I want chicken.
*   It is delicious.
*   It is too hot.

Dialogue:

*   What do you want to eat?
*   I want rice and chicken.
*   Do you want water?
*   Yes, please.

* * *

Unit 56: Likes and dislikes
---------------------------

Expressions:

*   I like tea.
*   I don’t like coffee.
*   I love fruit.
*   I don’t want spicy food.

Dialogue:

*   Do you like fish?
*   Yes, I do.
*   Do you want soup?
*   No, thank you.

* * *

Module 4D: Shopping
-------------------

Unit 57: In a shop
------------------

Expressions:

*   How much is it?
*   I want this.
*   I want that one.
*   Too expensive.
*   Do you have a small one?
*   Thank you.

Dialogue:

*   Can I help you?
*   I want this.
*   How much is it?
*   Ten dollars.

* * *

Unit 58: Numbers and money
--------------------------

Expressions:

*   one, two, three...
*   ten, twenty, thirty...
*   cheap
*   expensive
*   money
*   change

Dialogue:

*   How much is it?
*   Twenty.
*   Okay.
*   Thank you.

* * *

Module 4E: Travel and outside
-----------------------------

Unit 59: Going somewhere
------------------------

Expressions:

*   Let’s go.
*   I am going home.
*   Come with me.
*   Wait here.
*   Stop here.

Dialogue:

*   Where are you going?
*   I am going home.
*   Wait here.
*   Okay.

* * *

Unit 60: Asking directions
--------------------------

Expressions:

*   Where is the bathroom?
*   Where is the station?
*   Turn left.
*   Turn right.
*   Go straight.

Dialogue:

*   Excuse me, where is the bathroom?
*   Go straight.
*   Turn left.
*   Thank you.

* * *

Module 4F: Phone and communication
----------------------------------

Unit 61: Phone basics
---------------------

Expressions:

*   Hello?
*   Can you hear me?
*   I can hear you.
*   I can’t hear you.
*   Say it again.
*   Call me later.

Dialogue:

*   Hello?
*   Can you hear me?
*   Yes, I can hear you.
*   Okay, talk later.

* * *

Unit 66: Clothes
----------------

*   pants
*   shoes

Unit 67: Colors
---------------

Words:

*   red
*   blue
*   green
*   black
*   white
*   yellow
*   pink

Sentences:

*   I like blue.
*   The bag is black.
*   The flower is pink.

* * *

Unit 68: Simple past introduction
---------------------------------

Keep it light.

Words:

*   yesterday
*   went
*   ate
*   saw
*   came

Sentences:

*   I went home.
*   I ate rice.
*   I saw him yesterday.

* * *

Unit 69: Simple future introduction
-----------------------------------

Words:

*   tomorrow
*   will
*   later
*   soon

Sentences:

*   I will go tomorrow.
*   See you later.
*   I will call you.

* * *

Unit 70: Review and free speaking
---------------------------------

Goal:

*   answer basic questions without reading

Questions:

*   What is your name?
*   Where are you from?
*   Are you hungry?
*   What do you want?
*   What do you like?
*   Where is your bag?
*   How are you?

Pronunciation track for Thai learners
=====================================

This should run beside the main course.

Track P1: Final consonants
--------------------------

Practice:

*   cap / cab
*   back / bag
*   rice / ride
*   pick / pig
*   bet / bed

* * *

Track P2: R and L
-----------------

Practice:

*   right / light
*   long / wrong
*   fly / fry
*   glass / grass

* * *

Track P3: V and W
-----------------

Practice:

*   vest / west
*   vine / wine
*   very / wary

* * *

Track P4: TH
------------

Practice:

*   tin / thin
*   tank / thank
*   day / they
*   den / then

* * *

Track P5: Stress and rhythm
---------------------------

Practice:

*   WAter
*   TAble
*   BAby
*   toMOrrow
*   baNAna

Sentence rhythm:

*   I WANT WAter.
*   THIS is my TAble.
*   WHERE is the BATHroom?

* * *

Core vocabulary target
======================

By end of beginner course:

*   300 to 500 words
*   60 to 100 sentence patterns
*   100+ mini dialogues
*   basic daily speaking ability

* * *

Suggested first 150 words
=========================

People
------

I, you, he, she, we, they, it, mother, father, husband, wife, friend, baby, family

Actions
-------

go, come, eat, drink, sleep, sit, stand, walk, look, listen, speak, say, read, write, want, need, like, love, help, open, close, give, take, wait, stop

Home
----

house, home, room, bed, chair, table, door, window, kitchen, bathroom

Food
----

rice, water, food, tea, coffee, milk, juice, chicken, fish, egg, soup, noodle, bread, fruit

Feelings
--------

happy, sad, tired, hungry, thirsty, sick, okay, fine

Describing
----------

big, small, hot, cold, good, bad, new, old, long, short, fast, slow

Questions
---------

what, where, who, when, why, how

Time
----

today, tomorrow, yesterday, now, later, morning, afternoon, evening, night

Useful
------

yes, no, please, thank you, sorry, hello, goodbye, here, there, this, that

Numbers
-------

one to twenty, thirty, forty, fifty, hundred

Places
------

shop, school, hospital, station, road, market, car, bus

* * *

Voice-to-voice curriculum format
================================

For every lesson, add this speaking flow:

Step 1: Listen only
-------------------

Example:

*   “water”
*   “rice”
*   “I want water.”

Step 2: Repeat
--------------

Learner repeats after each model

Step 3: Syllable repeat
-----------------------

*   wa-ter
*   ri-ce

Step 4: Meaning check
---------------------

*   water = น้ำ
*   rice = ข้าว

Step 5: Controlled speaking
---------------------------

Prompt:

*   Say: “I want water.”
*   Say: “I want rice.”

Step 6: Guided dialogue
-----------------------

App:

*   What do you want?  
    User:
*   I want water.

Step 7: Free answer
-------------------

App:

*   What do you want to drink?  
    User speaks own answer.

* * *

Weekly plan
===========

Weeks 1–2
---------

*   sounds
*   vowels
*   easy consonants
*   20 words
*   10 sentences

Weeks 3–4
---------

*   final consonants
*   one-syllable words
*   food and home words
*   I want / I like / This is

Weeks 5–6
---------

*   family
*   daily actions
*   feelings
*   Where is / What is / Who is

Weeks 7–8
---------

*   shopping
*   numbers
*   time
*   asking for help
*   simple conversations

Weeks 9–10
----------

*   harder sounds
*   r/l, v/w, th
*   travel and phone
*   longer dialogues

Weeks 11–12
-----------

*   review
*   automatic speaking
*   daily conversation drills
*   free speaking with support

* * *

Example lesson template
=======================

Lesson title
------------

Water and Rice

### Sound focus

W / R

### Syllables

wa, wo, ra, ri

### Words

*   water
*   rice
*   want
*   hot
*   good

### Meaning

*   water = น้ำ
*   rice = ข้าว
*   want = ต้องการ
*   hot = ร้อน
*   good = ดี

### Sentences

*   I want water.
*   I want rice.
*   The rice is hot.
*   It is good.

### Voice practice

*   Repeat “water”
*   Repeat “rice”
*   Say “I want water”
*   Answer: “What do you want?”

### Dialogue

*   What do you want?
*   I want water.
*   Do you want rice?
*   Yes, please.

* * *

Review system
=============

Every 5 lessons:

*   review old words
*   review old sounds
*   quick speaking test
*   listen and choose
*   say the sentence from memory

Review types:

1.  hear and repeat
2.  hear and choose meaning
3.  see picture and speak
4.  answer question with voice
5.  fix wrong pronunciation

* * *

Final beginner outcomes
=======================

At the end, she should be able to:

*   understand very common words
*   say simple daily needs
*   ask for food, water, help, directions
*   introduce herself
*   describe simple feelings
*   answer short questions
*   handle very basic daily conversation

* * *

Best teaching method for her
============================

For your wife, the best order is:

**Thai meaning → English sound → repetition → simple sentence → voice response**

Not:

*   grammar rules first
*   spelling first
*   long vocabulary lists
*   complicated explanations

Keep everything:

*   short
*   spoken
*   repeated
*   useful

* * *

I can next turn this into a **complete 12-week lesson-by-lesson curriculum**, with every lesson showing:

*   sound focus
*   word list
*   Thai meaning
*   sentences
*   voice drills
*   mini-dialogues

## Prompt:

## Response:
07/04/2026, 20:47:41

> Thought for 26s

Here is the **complete 12-week beginner curriculum**, lesson by lesson, for a Thai-speaking absolute beginner.

Use it as:

*   app curriculum
*   printed workbook
*   teaching plan
*   voice lesson script

Each week has **5 lessons + 1 review day + 1 light practice day**.

Best daily time:

*   **15 to 20 minutes**
*   speaking every lesson
*   no long grammar explanations

* * *

12-Week Beginner English Course
===============================

Daily lesson structure
----------------------

Every lesson should follow this order:

1.  **Sound focus**
2.  **Syllable practice**
3.  **5 new words**
4.  **2 to 4 short sentences**
5.  **Voice repeat**
6.  **Mini dialogue**
7.  **Review old words**

* * *

WEEK 1 — FIRST SOUNDS AND FIRST WORDS
=====================================

Goal
----

*   get comfortable with English sounds
*   learn classroom-style and home-style first words
*   begin “This is…” and “I want…”

* * *

Lesson 1
--------

### Sound focus

a / e

### Syllables

ba, be, ma, me, ta, te

### Words

*   bag = กระเป๋า
*   bed = เตียง
*   map = แผนที่
*   pen = ปากกา
*   cat = แมว

### Sentences

*   This is a bag.
*   This is a pen.

### Voice practice

*   say: bag
*   say: bed
*   say: This is a bag.

### Mini dialogue

*   What is this?
*   It is a bag.

* * *

Lesson 2
--------

### Sound focus

i / o

### Syllables

bi, bo, mi, mo, ti, to

### Words

*   sit = นั่ง
*   book = หนังสือ
*   dog = สุนัข
*   box = กล่อง
*   big = ใหญ่

### Sentences

*   Sit down.
*   The dog is big.

### Voice practice

*   say: sit
*   say: book
*   say: The dog is big.

### Mini dialogue

*   What is this?
*   It is a book.

* * *

Lesson 3
--------

### Sound focus

u / short vowels review

### Syllables

bu, mu, tu, su

### Words

*   cup = ถ้วย
*   bus = รถบัส
*   sun = ดวงอาทิตย์
*   room = ห้อง
*   good = ดี

### Sentences

*   This is a cup.
*   The room is good.

### Voice practice

*   say: cup
*   say: good
*   say: This is a cup.

### Mini dialogue

*   Is this your cup?
*   Yes, it is.

* * *

Lesson 4
--------

### Sound focus

b / p / m

### Syllables

ba, pa, ma, be, pe, me

### Words

*   baby = เด็กทารก
*   pen = ปากกา
*   mom = แม่
*   map = แผนที่
*   paper = กระดาษ

### Sentences

*   This is my mom.
*   This is paper.

### Voice practice

*   baby
*   mom
*   pen
*   This is my mom.

### Mini dialogue

*   Who is she?
*   She is my mom.

* * *

Lesson 5
--------

### Sound focus

t / d / n

### Words

*   ten = สิบ
*   door = ประตู
*   nose = จมูก
*   day = วัน
*   tea = ชา

### Sentences

*   Open the door.
*   I want tea.

### Voice practice

*   door
*   tea
*   I want tea.

### Mini dialogue

*   What do you want?
*   I want tea.

* * *

Day 6 review
------------

Review:

*   bag, bed, pen, cat, sit, book, dog, cup, tea, door

Sentence review:

*   This is a bag.
*   This is a cup.
*   I want tea.
*   Open the door.

Listening:

*   choose the word you hear

Speaking:

*   answer “What is this?”
*   answer “What do you want?”

* * *

Day 7 light practice
--------------------

Only:

*   repeat all words
*   listen and copy
*   simple picture speaking

* * *

---------

### Words

*   hungry = หิว
*   thirsty = กระหาย
*   sick = ไม่สบาย
*   sleepy = ง่วง
*   ready = พร้อม

### Sentences

*   I am hungry.
*   I am thirsty.
*   I feel sick.

* * *

Lesson 23
---------

### Pattern focus

*   I am \_\_\_.
*   Are you \_\_\_?

### Practice

*   happy
*   tired
*   hungry
*   okay
*   ready

### Mini dialogue

*   Are you okay?
*   Yes, I am.
*   Are you tired?
*   Yes, I am.

* * *

Lesson 24
---------

### Words

*   help = ช่วย
*   need = ต้องการ
*   want = อยาก
*   please = กรุณา
*   thank you = ขอบคุณ

### Sentences

*   I need help.
*   Please help me.
*   Thank you.

* * *

Lesson 25
---------

### Survival expressions

*   I am hungry.
*   I want water.
*   I need help.
*   Please.
*   Thank you.

### Mini dialogue

*   Are you hungry?
*   Yes, I am.
*   What do you want?
*   I want rice.

hear last sound clearly

Lesson 60
---------

### Final speaking test

Questions:

*   What is your name?
*   How are you?
*   Are you hungry?
*   What do you want?
*   Who is he?
*   Where is your bag?
*   Do you like coffee?
*   Can you help me?
*   Where is the bathroom?
*   What do you do in the morning?

Target:  
answer every question in 1 short sentence

* * *

Weekly review format
====================

At the end of each week, do 5 review activities:

1\. Listen and repeat
---------------------

Play 10 old words

2\. Picture speaking
--------------------

Show picture, learner says word

3\. Sentence completion
-----------------------

Example:

*   I want \_\_\_.
*   This is my \_\_\_.

4\. Voice answer
----------------

App asks:

*   What do you want?
*   Where are you?

5\. Pronunciation correction
----------------------------

Repeat hard sounds:

*   r/l
*   v/w
*   th
*   final consonants

* * *

Core sentence patterns to master
================================

By the end of the course, she should know these patterns very well:

*   This is \_\_\_.
*   That is \_\_\_.
*   It is \_\_\_.
*   I am \_\_\_.
*   You are \_\_\_.
*   He is \_\_\_.
*   She is \_\_\_.
*   I want \_\_\_.
*   I need \_\_\_.
*   I like \_\_\_.
*   I don’t like \_\_\_.
*   Do you want \_\_\_?
*   What is this?
*   Who is he?
*   Where is \_\_\_?
*   Can you help me?
*   I don’t understand.
*   Please say it again.
*   Speak slowly, please.
*   How much is it?

* * *

Best word order for app/database entry
======================================

For each word, store:

*   English word
*   Thai meaning
*   syllable split
*   pronunciation guide
*   example sentence
*   slow audio
*   normal audio
*   learner recording
*   related picture
*   category
*   lesson number

Example:

**water**

*   Thai: น้ำ
*   syllables: wa-ter
*   pronunciation: WAW-ter
*   sentence: I want water.
*   category: drink
*   lesson: 9

* * *

Best dialogue format for voice-to-voice
=======================================

Each dialogue should have 3 modes:

Mode 1: repeat after audio
--------------------------

App says:

*   I want water.

Learner repeats.

Mode 2: guided response
-----------------------

App asks:

*   What do you want?

Expected answer:

*   I want water.

Mode 3: open response
---------------------

App asks:

*   What do you want to drink?

Learner can answer:

*   I want tea.
*   I want water.

* * *

Best milestone targets
======================

End of week 4
-------------

She can:

*   name home objects
*   use this/that
*   say simple wants

End of week 8
-------------

She can:

*   answer basic questions
*   ask for food, help, objects
*   do very short conversation

End of week 12
--------------

She can:

*   introduce herself
*   talk about home, food, family
*   ask basic directions
*   handle very beginner daily English

* * *

What to avoid
=============

Do not teach early:

*   long grammar rules
*   alphabet spelling tests
*   irregular verbs as theory
*   big vocabulary lists
*   full paragraph reading

Teach:

*   small spoken chunks
*   lots of repetition
*   voice interaction
*   real daily life English

* * *

Next step should be to turn this into a **lesson production pack**, where each of the 60 lessons includes the exact:

*   word list
*   Thai meanings
*   example sentences
*   voice prompts
*   mini-dialogue script
*   review quiz items

## Prompt:
07/04/2026, 20:52:34

complete app specification with screens, features, and database structure.

## Response:
07/04/2026, 20:52:35

I’m converting the curriculum into a buildable product spec: user flow, screen inventory, feature set, backend schema, and voice pipeline. I’ll keep it structured so it can go straight to a designer or developer.

> Thought for 6s

Below is a **complete app specification** for a **beginner English learning app for a Thai speaker**, focused on:

*   starting from zero
*   pronunciation first
*   syllables
*   small common words
*   Thai meaning support
*   voice-to-voice practice
*   short daily lessons

This is written so it can be used by:

*   app designer
*   frontend developer
*   backend developer
*   content team
*   speech/AI engineer

* * *

1\. Product overview
====================

Product name
------------

Working name: **Easy English Thai**

Product goal
------------

Teach a Thai-speaking adult with little or no English how to:

*   hear English sounds
*   pronounce them clearly
*   understand common words
*   speak short daily sentences
*   hold very basic voice conversations

Target user
-----------

Primary user:

*   Thai-speaking adult beginner
*   low confidence in English
*   prefers audio over text
*   learns best with repetition and Thai explanations

Secondary use case:

*   husband/partner helping learner practice
*   home-based daily learning

Core learning method
--------------------

The app teaches in this order:

1.  sound
2.  syllable
3.  word
4.  sentence
5.  guided speaking
6.  voice conversation
7.  review

Product principles
------------------

*   mobile-first
*   very simple UI
*   Thai support everywhere
*   minimal grammar explanation
*   audio-heavy
*   short sessions
*   repeat often
*   strong pronunciation support

* * *

2\. Primary use cases
=====================

Use case 1: Daily beginner lesson
---------------------------------

User opens app and completes a 10–15 minute lesson:

*   hears sounds
*   repeats
*   learns 5 words
*   says 2–3 sentences
*   answers a simple spoken question

Use case 2: Pronunciation practice
----------------------------------

User selects a difficult sound:

*   r/l
*   v/w
*   th
*   final consonants

Then practices listening and repeating.

Use case 3: Word review
-----------------------

User reviews words learned previously with:

*   picture
*   Thai meaning
*   audio
*   repeat
*   quiz
*   voice response

Use case 4: Mini voice conversation
-----------------------------------

User does a short roleplay:

*   greeting
*   asking for water
*   shopping
*   saying “I am tired”
*   asking for help

Use case 5: Free speaking support
---------------------------------

User taps mic and answers simple prompts:

*   What is your name?
*   What do you want?
*   Are you hungry?

* * *

3\. Platform scope
==================

MVP platforms
-------------

*   iOS
*   Android

Recommended frontend
--------------------

*   Flutter

Reason:

*   one codebase
*   strong audio support
*   good mobile performance
*   efficient for cross-platform product

Recommended backend
-------------------

*   Firebase or Supabase

Recommended choice for MVP:

*   **Firebase** if speed of implementation is the priority
*   **Supabase** if relational querying and SQL-first schema is preferred

Recommended architecture
------------------------

*   client app
*   content API / database
*   speech services
*   analytics
*   cloud storage for audio/image assets

* * *

4\. User roles
==============

4.1 Learner
-----------

Main role.  
Can:

*   take lessons
*   review vocabulary
*   do pronunciation practice
*   do voice dialogues
*   track progress

4.2 Support partner
-------------------

Optional second role.  
Can:

*   see learner progress
*   start shared practice mode
*   trigger partner conversation prompts

4.3 Admin
---------

Can:

*   manage curriculum
*   upload words/audio/images
*   edit lessons
*   manage dialogues
*   review analytics

4.4 Content editor
------------------

Can:

*   create words
*   assign Thai meanings
*   add sentences
*   add audio
*   tag pronunciation difficulty

* * *

5\. Core feature set
====================

5.1 Onboarding
--------------

Purpose:

*   set language
*   determine learner level
*   explain learning style

Features:

*   choose interface language: Thai / English / bilingual
*   choose learner name
*   choose lesson pace: slow / normal
*   choose goal: daily life / travel / home conversation
*   initial pronunciation diagnostic
*   optional partner setup

5.2 Daily lesson engine
-----------------------

Features:

*   short daily lesson
*   lesson steps locked in sequence
*   one-tap replay
*   slow playback
*   record and compare
*   sentence speaking check
*   end-of-lesson score
*   lesson completion badge

5.3 Sound training
------------------

Features:

*   individual phoneme practice
*   mouth-position hints
*   minimal pair practice
*   difficult Thai-speaker sound sets
*   slow audio
*   loop playback

5.4 Syllable training
---------------------

Features:

*   consonant-vowel drills
*   one-syllable training
*   two-syllable stress practice
*   syllable segmentation display
*   clap/stress mode for rhythm

5.5 Vocabulary training
-----------------------

Features:

*   word card
*   Thai meaning
*   image
*   audio
*   syllable split
*   example sentence
*   repeat mode
*   review mode
*   “hard words” saved automatically

5.6 Sentence pattern training
-----------------------------

Features:

*   sentence frames
*   substitution drills
*   fill with picture
*   say full sentence aloud
*   guided correction

5.7 Voice-to-voice mode
-----------------------

Features:

*   app speaks prompt
*   learner responds by voice
*   speech recognition
*   response validation
*   pronunciation feedback
*   retry flow
*   simple branching dialogue

5.8 Review and spaced repetition
--------------------------------

Features:

*   daily review queue
*   weak-word resurfacing
*   weak-sound resurfacing
*   weekly recap
*   mastery scoring

5.9 Progress tracking
---------------------

Features:

*   lessons completed
*   words learned
*   pronunciation improvement
*   streak
*   confidence metrics
*   sound difficulty heatmap

5.10 Offline learning
---------------------

MVP optional, version 2 preferred.  
Features:

*   download lessons/audio packs
*   offline playback
*   offline lesson completion sync later

* * *

6\. Learning model and lesson structure
=======================================

Lesson structure
----------------

Each lesson contains:

1.  intro
2.  sound focus
3.  syllable drill
4.  5 target words
5.  2–4 target sentences
6.  guided speaking
7.  mini dialogue
8.  review check
9.  completion screen

Example lesson object
---------------------

Lesson 9:

*   sound focus: w
*   words: water, we, yes, you, yellow
*   sentences:
    *   I want water.
    *   Yes, please.
*   dialogue:
    *   Do you want water?
    *   Yes, please.

Content hierarchy
-----------------

*   Course
*   Level
*   Module
*   Unit
*   Lesson
*   Step
*   Exercise
*   Asset

* * *

7\. Screen specification
========================

7.1 Splash screen
-----------------

Purpose:

*   branding
*   app loading
*   auth check

Elements:

*   logo
*   short tagline
*   loading indicator

* * *

7.2 Language selection screen
-----------------------------

Purpose:

*   set UI language

Elements:

*   Thai
*   English
*   bilingual toggle
*   continue button

Behavior:

*   default to Thai for this product

* * *

7.3 Welcome / onboarding intro
------------------------------

Purpose:

*   explain app style simply

Elements:

*   short slides:
    *   learn by listening
    *   repeat and speak
    *   small daily lessons
*   continue button
*   skip button

* * *

7.4 Account setup screen
------------------------

Fields:

*   learner name
*   age range optional
*   native language
*   learning goal
*   daily reminder time optional

* * *

7.5 Level check screen
----------------------

Purpose:

*   detect if user is truly beginner

Sections:

*   can you understand these words?
*   can you say your name in English?
*   hear and repeat sample
*   optional skip

Output:

*   recommended starting level

For your target user:

*   likely Level 0

* * *

7.6 Home screen
---------------

Purpose:  
main hub

Sections:

*   today’s lesson card
*   continue where you left off
*   review due today
*   pronunciation practice shortcut
*   recent words
*   streak / progress summary

Buttons:

*   Start lesson
*   Review
*   Sounds
*   Speak
*   Profile

Navigation:  
bottom tab bar

* * *

7.7 Lesson player screen
------------------------

This is the most important screen.

### Layout

Top:

*   lesson title
*   progress bar
*   exit button

Center:

*   current content area

Bottom:

*   replay
*   slow audio
*   mic
*   next

### Dynamic content based on step type

Possible content blocks:

*   sound display
*   syllable row
*   word card
*   sentence card
*   image prompt
*   dialogue prompt

### Step types

*   listen-only
*   repeat-after-me
*   syllable tap
*   choose meaning
*   speak sentence
*   answer question
*   dialogue turn

* * *

7.8 Sound practice screen
-------------------------

Purpose:  
practice phonemes and contrast pairs

Elements:

*   sound category tabs
*   target sound card
*   mouth hint diagram
*   examples list
*   compare pair button
*   record button

Categories:

*   vowels
*   easy consonants
*   hard consonants
*   Thai learner problem sounds
*   final consonants

* * *

7.9 Minimal pairs screen
------------------------

Purpose:  
help with hard distinctions

Examples:

*   right / light
*   fan / van
*   tin / thin
*   west / vest

Elements:

*   play word A
*   play word B
*   choose what you heard
*   repeat word A
*   repeat word B

* * *

7.10 Word detail screen
-----------------------

Purpose:  
show one word deeply

Fields:

*   word
*   Thai meaning
*   syllable split
*   pronunciation guide
*   audio normal
*   audio slow
*   image
*   example sentence
*   record yourself
*   mastery status

Buttons:

*   add to favorites
*   practice word
*   next word

* * *

7.11 Vocabulary review screen
-----------------------------

Modes:

*   flashcard
*   picture-to-word
*   audio-to-meaning
*   say the word
*   say the sentence

Filters:

*   today due
*   difficult words
*   lesson words
*   category words

* * *

7.12 Sentence pattern screen
----------------------------

Purpose:  
practice reusable structures

Example pattern:

*   I want \_\_\_.

Elements:

*   pattern header
*   substitution words
*   example sentences
*   speak sentence
*   prompt-and-answer practice

* * *

7.13 Dialogue practice screen
-----------------------------

Purpose:  
guided voice-to-voice speaking

Modes:

*   listen and repeat
*   guided response
*   open answer

Display:

*   character bubble or clean simple speech UI
*   app prompt text
*   Thai support translation toggle
*   mic response area
*   transcript of learner attempt
*   correctness feedback

* * *

7.14 Pronunciation feedback screen
----------------------------------

Purpose:  
show result after speaking

Metrics:

*   overall score
*   sound accuracy
*   stress accuracy
*   final consonant check
*   fluency basic check

Feedback examples:

*   good
*   try final sound again
*   stress first syllable
*   say “water” more slowly

Important:  
feedback should be simple, not technical

* * *

7.15 Weekly review screen
-------------------------

Sections:

*   words learned
*   sounds to practice
*   sentence patterns mastered
*   quick speaking test
*   week complete badge

* * *

7.16 Progress dashboard screen
------------------------------

Metrics:

*   total lessons completed
*   total words learned
*   speaking score trend
*   review completion
*   current streak
*   hardest sounds
*   mastered categories

Graphs:

*   simple, not cluttered

* * *

7.17 Practice mode hub
----------------------

Options:

*   Sounds
*   Words
*   Sentences
*   Dialogues
*   Hard words
*   Partner practice

* * *

7.18 Partner practice screen
----------------------------

Optional feature.

Purpose:  
support practice with husband/partner

Modes:

*   listen together
*   repeat together
*   question cards
*   roleplay scripts

Prompts:

*   Ask: “What do you want?”
*   Ask: “Are you hungry?”
*   Ask: “Where is the bag?”

* * *

7.19 Settings screen
--------------------

Options:

*   interface language
*   audio speed default
*   male/female voice
*   subtitles on/off
*   Thai meaning on/off
*   daily reminder
*   download lessons
*   delete recordings

* * *

7.20 Admin CMS screens
----------------------

Web admin recommended.

Core screens:

*   courses
*   lessons
*   words
*   audio assets
*   images
*   dialogues
*   review queue rules
*   analytics dashboard

* * *

8\. Navigation structure
========================

Bottom tab navigation
---------------------

*   Home
*   Review
*   Sounds
*   Speak
*   Profile

Internal lesson flow
--------------------

*   Home → Today’s lesson → Lesson step sequence → Completion → Review recommendation

Practice flow
-------------

*   Home → Practice → choose mode → exercise sequence

* * *

9\. Functional specification
============================

9.1 Authentication
------------------

Options:

*   anonymous guest mode
*   email login
*   phone login
*   social login optional

Recommendation:

*   allow guest mode first
*   encourage account creation later

9.2 User profile
----------------

Data:

*   name
*   UI language
*   learning pace
*   goal
*   current level
*   current lesson
*   streak
*   reminder settings

9.3 Content delivery
--------------------

Requirements:

*   versioned lesson content
*   content pulled from backend
*   assets cached locally
*   localized text support
*   downloadable content bundles

9.4 Audio playback
------------------

Requirements:

*   fast load
*   normal speed
*   slow speed
*   replay instantly
*   queue for sequential exercises

9.5 Recording
-------------

Requirements:

*   record user speech
*   playback recording
*   upload for assessment
*   optionally store locally only if privacy mode is enabled

9.6 Speech recognition
----------------------

Purpose:

*   capture spoken response
*   determine if intended answer is correct

Needs:

*   English ASR
*   tolerant to beginner accent
*   intent-based matching for open-ended exercises

9.7 Pronunciation assessment
----------------------------

Purpose:

*   score how close the learner’s speech is to target pronunciation

Check:

*   phoneme accuracy
*   word-level accuracy
*   stress
*   final consonant presence
*   timing basic check

9.8 Dialogue engine
-------------------

Must support:

*   scripted dialogues
*   expected answers
*   alternate valid answers
*   branching paths
*   repeat on failure
*   hints after wrong response

9.9 Spaced repetition engine
----------------------------

Should track:

*   word difficulty
*   sound difficulty
*   sentence difficulty
*   review due date
*   incorrect history
*   speaking confidence

9.10 Analytics
--------------

Track:

*   lesson starts
*   lesson completions
*   step drop-off
*   replay count
*   mic usage
*   pronunciation retries
*   average word accuracy
*   top difficult sounds

* * *

10\. Voice-to-voice system specification
========================================

10.1 Voice flow types
---------------------

### Type A: repeat-after-model

App:

*   “water”

Learner:

*   repeats “water”

System:

*   scores pronunciation

### Type B: guided answer

App:

*   “What do you want?”

Expected:

*   “I want water.”
*   “I want tea.”
*   “I want rice.”

System:

*   validates response structure and target words

### Type C: choice then speak

App shows image of water.  
App asks:

*   “What is this?”

Expected:

*   “It is water.”

### Type D: mini conversation

App:

*   “Are you hungry?”  
    Learner:
*   “Yes, I am.”  
    App:
*   “What do you want to eat?”  
    Learner:
*   “I want rice.”

10.2 Dialogue validation types
------------------------------

*   exact answer match
*   synonym match
*   slot-based match
*   semantic intent match
*   pronunciation threshold match

10.3 Feedback rules
-------------------

Feedback must be:

*   short
*   supportive
*   actionable

Examples:

*   Good job.
*   Try again.
*   Say the last sound.
*   Say it more slowly.
*   Stress the first part: WA-ter.

* * *

12\. Database structure
=======================

I’ll define this in relational form. This works well in PostgreSQL or Supabase. It can also map to Firestore collections with some denormalization.

* * *

12.1 Users table
----------------

**users**

*   id UUID PK
*   email nullable
*   phone nullable
*   display\_name
*   native\_language
*   interface\_language
*   learning\_goal
*   current\_level\_id
*   current\_lesson\_id
*   daily\_reminder\_time nullable
*   voice\_speed\_preference
*   thai\_translation\_enabled boolean
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.2 User settings table
------------------------

**user\_settings**

*   id UUID PK
*   user\_id FK users.id
*   preferred\_voice\_gender
*   audio\_speed\_default
*   subtitles\_enabled
*   offline\_mode\_enabled
*   notifications\_enabled
*   privacy\_mode\_enabled
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.3 Courses table
------------------

**courses**

*   id UUID PK
*   title
*   description
*   target\_language
*   source\_language
*   version
*   is\_published
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.4 Levels table
-----------------

**levels**

*   id UUID PK
*   course\_id FK courses.id
*   level\_order
*   title
*   description
*   CEFR\_like\_label nullable
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.5 Modules table
------------------

**modules**

*   id UUID PK
*   level\_id FK levels.id
*   module\_order
*   title
*   description
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.6 Units table
----------------

**units**

*   id UUID PK
*   module\_id FK modules.id
*   unit\_order
*   title
*   description
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.7 Lessons table
------------------

**lessons**

*   id UUID PK
*   unit\_id FK units.id
*   lesson\_order
*   title
*   subtitle nullable
*   estimated\_minutes
*   lesson\_type
*   sound\_focus\_id nullable FK sounds.id
*   is\_review\_lesson boolean
*   is\_published boolean
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.8 Exercise steps table
-------------------------

**lesson\_steps**

*   id UUID PK
*   lesson\_id FK lessons.id
*   step\_order
*   step\_type
*   title nullable
*   instruction\_en
*   instruction\_th
*   payload\_json
*   passing\_rule\_json
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

`payload_json` may contain:

*   word ids
*   sentence ids
*   image ids
*   audio ids
*   dialogue config
*   answer expectations

* * *

12.9 Sounds table
-----------------

**sounds**

*   id UUID PK
*   sound\_code
*   display\_symbol
*   title
*   description\_en
*   description\_th
*   mouth\_hint
*   category
*   thai\_difficulty\_flag boolean
*   audio\_demo\_normal\_url
*   audio\_demo\_slow\_url
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.10 Words table
-----------------

**words**

*   id UUID PK
*   english\_text
*   thai\_text
*   transliteration nullable
*   pronunciation\_hint
*   ipa nullable
*   syllable\_split
*   part\_of\_speech
*   category
*   difficulty\_level
*   frequency\_rank nullable
*   image\_asset\_id nullable
*   audio\_normal\_asset\_id nullable
*   audio\_slow\_asset\_id nullable
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.11 Sentences table
---------------------

**sentences**

*   id UUID PK
*   english\_text
*   thai\_text
*   pronunciation\_hint nullable
*   ipa nullable
*   sentence\_pattern\_id nullable
*   difficulty\_level
*   audio\_normal\_asset\_id nullable
*   audio\_slow\_asset\_id nullable
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.12 Sentence patterns table
-----------------------------

**sentence\_patterns**

*   id UUID PK
*   pattern\_text
*   pattern\_text\_th
*   explanation\_th
*   difficulty\_level
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

Examples:

*   I want \_\_\_.
*   This is \_\_\_.
*   Where is \_\_\_?

* * *

12.13 Dialogues table
---------------------

**dialogues**

*   id UUID PK
*   title
*   description
*   level\_id FK levels.id
*   context\_type
*   mode
*   turns\_json
*   validation\_json
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

* * *

12.14 Assets table
------------------

**assets**

*   id UUID PK
*   asset\_type
*   url
*   localizable\_key nullable
*   duration\_ms nullable
*   metadata\_json
*   created\_at
*   updated\_at

asset\_type examples:

*   image
*   audio\_normal
*   audio\_slow
*   mouth\_diagram
*   icon

* * *

12.15 Lesson-word join table
----------------------------

**lesson\_words**

*   lesson\_id FK lessons.id
*   word\_id FK words.id
*   display\_order  
    PK:
*   lesson\_id
*   word\_id

* * *

12.16 Lesson-sentence join table
--------------------------------

**lesson\_sentences**

*   lesson\_id FK lessons.id
*   sentence\_id FK sentences.id
*   display\_order  
    PK:
*   lesson\_id
*   sentence\_id

* * *

12.17 Word-sound join table
---------------------------

**word\_sounds**

*   word\_id FK words.id
*   sound\_id FK sounds.id  
    PK:
*   word\_id
*   sound\_id

* * *

12.18 Minimal pair groups
-------------------------

**minimal\_pair\_groups**

*   id UUID PK
*   title
*   sound\_a\_id FK sounds.id
*   sound\_b\_id FK sounds.id
*   created\_at

**minimal\_pair\_items**

*   id UUID PK
*   group\_id FK minimal\_pair\_groups.id
*   word\_a\_id FK words.id
*   word\_b\_id FK words.id
*   audio\_a\_asset\_id nullable
*   audio\_b\_asset\_id nullable

* * *

12.19 User progress by lesson
-----------------------------

**user\_lesson\_progress**

*   id UUID PK
*   user\_id FK users.id
*   lesson\_id FK lessons.id
*   status
*   started\_at
*   completed\_at nullable
*   score\_overall nullable
*   pronunciation\_score nullable
*   comprehension\_score nullable
*   retry\_count default 0
*   time\_spent\_seconds default 0

* * *

12.20 User progress by word
---------------------------

**user\_word\_progress**

*   id UUID PK
*   user\_id FK users.id
*   word\_id FK words.id
*   familiarity\_score
*   pronunciation\_score
*   listening\_score
*   speaking\_score
*   times\_seen
*   times\_correct
*   times\_incorrect
*   last\_seen\_at
*   next\_review\_at nullable
*   is\_hard\_word boolean default false

* * *

12.21 User progress by sound
----------------------------

**user\_sound\_progress**

*   id UUID PK
*   user\_id FK users.id
*   sound\_id FK sounds.id
*   accuracy\_score
*   attempts\_count
*   last\_practiced\_at
*   next\_review\_at nullable
*   difficulty\_flag boolean default false

* * *

12.22 User speaking attempts
----------------------------

**user\_speaking\_attempts**

*   id UUID PK
*   user\_id FK users.id
*   lesson\_step\_id nullable FK lesson\_steps.id
*   word\_id nullable FK words.id
*   sentence\_id nullable FK sentences.id
*   dialogue\_id nullable FK dialogues.id
*   recording\_asset\_id nullable FK assets.id
*   transcript\_text nullable
*   recognition\_confidence nullable
*   pronunciation\_score nullable
*   phoneme\_feedback\_json nullable
*   feedback\_text
*   created\_at

* * *

12.23 Review queue
------------------

**review\_queue**

*   id UUID PK
*   user\_id FK users.id
*   content\_type
*   content\_id
*   due\_at
*   priority
*   source\_reason
*   created\_at
*   completed\_at nullable

content\_type:

*   word
*   sound
*   sentence
*   dialogue

* * *

12.24 Achievements
------------------

**achievements**

*   id UUID PK
*   code
*   title
*   description
*   icon\_asset\_id nullable

**user\_achievements**

*   id UUID PK
*   user\_id FK users.id
*   achievement\_id FK achievements.id
*   unlocked\_at

* * *

12.25 Analytics events
----------------------

**analytics\_events**

*   id UUID PK
*   user\_id nullable
*   event\_name
*   event\_properties\_json
*   created\_at

* * *

13\. Example data relationships
===============================

Example:

*   Lesson 9 has sound focus W
*   Lesson 9 links to word ids:
    *   water
    *   we
    *   yes
    *   you
    *   yellow
*   Lesson 9 links to sentence ids:
    *   I want water.
    *   Yes, please.
*   Lesson 9 has lesson steps:
    *   play sound
    *   syllable drill
    *   word flashcards
    *   sentence repeat
    *   dialogue turn

14\. API specification outline
==============================

Auth endpoints
--------------

*   POST /auth/signup
*   POST /auth/login
*   POST /auth/guest
*   POST /auth/logout

Content endpoints
-----------------

*   GET /courses
*   GET /courses/{id}
*   GET /lessons/{id}
*   GET /lessons/{id}/steps
*   GET /words/{id}
*   GET /sentences/{id}
*   GET /sounds/{id}
*   GET /dialogues/{id}

Progress endpoints
------------------

*   GET /me/progress
*   POST /lessons/{id}/start
*   POST /lessons/{id}/complete
*   POST /words/{id}/progress
*   POST /sounds/{id}/progress

Review endpoints
----------------

*   GET /me/review-queue
*   POST /review/{id}/complete

Speech endpoints
----------------

*   POST /speech/recognize
*   POST /speech/pronunciation-score
*   POST /dialogue/validate

Admin endpoints
---------------

*   POST /admin/lessons
*   PUT /admin/lessons/{id}
*   POST /admin/words
*   POST /admin/assets
*   POST /admin/dialogues

15\. Speech and AI system design
================================

15.1 Text-to-speech
-------------------

Needs:

*   natural English voice
*   slow mode
*   male/female option
*   consistent pronunciation

Use for:

*   sounds
*   words
*   sentences
*   dialogue prompts

15.2 Speech-to-text
-------------------

Needs:

*   beginner-accent tolerant English recognition
*   short utterance support
*   real-time or near-real-time result

Use for:

*   answering prompts
*   dialogue turns
*   capturing user transcript

15.3 Pronunciation scoring engine
---------------------------------

Needs:

*   phoneme-level or word-level pronunciation accuracy
*   stress detection for multisyllable words
*   final consonant detection
*   custom weighting for Thai learner pain points

15.4 Response validator
-----------------------

Needs:

*   exact and alternate answer matching
*   slot filling
*   semantic intent matching for short answers

Example:  
Prompt:

*   What do you want?

Valid:

*   I want water.
*   I want tea.
*   Water.  
    Depending on exercise strictness.

* * *

16\. Recommendation engine
==========================

Purpose
-------

Personalize practice based on weakness.

Inputs
------

*   missed words
*   low pronunciation scores
*   replay frequency
*   failed dialogue turns
*   unfinished lessons

Outputs
-------

*   today’s review queue
*   sound focus recommendation
*   repeat this lesson suggestion
*   weak word resurfacing

Rule examples:

*   if pronunciation\_score < 60 on 3 attempts, schedule sound review next day
*   if word missed twice, push into review queue within 24 hours
*   if sentence pattern repeatedly failed, assign pattern drill

* * *

17\. Content authoring rules
============================

Word rules
----------

Each word must have:

*   Thai meaning
*   one clear image if possible
*   normal audio
*   slow audio
*   syllable split
*   pronunciation hint
*   one simple sentence

Sentence rules
--------------

Each sentence must:

*   be short
*   use already taught words when possible
*   map to one reusable pattern
*   have Thai translation
*   have audio in slow and normal versions

Dialogue rules
--------------

Each dialogue must:

*   have a clear context
*   use very few new items
*   include expected answers
*   have retry hints
*   stay under 6 turns for beginner level

* * *

18\. UX rules for this audience
===============================

Must do
-------

*   large buttons
*   clear audio controls
*   one main action per screen
*   Thai translation visible or one tap away
*   minimal text clutter
*   strong use of icons and pictures

Must avoid
----------

*   dense grammar text
*   too many choices on one screen
*   long paragraphs
*   technical pronunciation labels by default
*   punishing red-error experiences

Feedback style
--------------

Use:

*   Good
*   Nice try
*   Try again slowly
*   Listen once more
*   Say the last sound

Avoid:

*   complex phonetic explanations unless advanced mode is enabled

* * *

19\. MVP scope
==============

Include in MVP
--------------

*   onboarding
*   daily lessons
*   audio playback
*   word cards
*   sentence practice
*   speaking recording
*   speech recognition
*   pronunciation scoring basic
*   review queue
*   progress dashboard basic
*   admin content upload
*   12-week curriculum

Exclude from MVP
----------------

*   live tutor mode
*   multiplayer
*   advanced grammar
*   video-based mouth analysis
*   offline full sync
*   partner remote linking
*   AI free conversation without guardrails

* * *

20\. Version 2 features
=======================

*   adaptive lesson difficulty
*   offline download packs
*   richer pronunciation visuals
*   partner mode with shared tracking
*   custom family vocabulary
*   Thai voice support for instructions
*   free conversation sandbox
*   teacher/admin web portal improvements

* * *

21\. Non-functional requirements
================================

Performance
-----------

*   lesson screen loads under 2 seconds on normal connection
*   audio starts within 500 ms after cache warm
*   speaking result returned within 2–4 seconds target

Reliability
-----------

*   recover from interrupted lesson
*   resume from last step
*   store progress safely

Accessibility
-------------

*   large text option
*   slower audio option
*   high contrast UI
*   captions/subtitles option

Privacy
-------

*   clear consent for mic usage
*   option to delete recordings
*   minimal retention policy
*   encrypt stored user audio

* * *

22\. Security requirements
==========================

*   secure auth tokens
*   encrypted API transport
*   protected audio upload endpoints
*   admin role access control
*   secure storage for recordings
*   audit logging for content edits

* * *

23\. Analytics KPIs
===================

Product KPIs
------------

*   day 1 retention
*   day 7 retention
*   lesson completion rate
*   daily active learners
*   weekly active learners
*   streak retention

Learning KPIs
-------------

*   average pronunciation score improvement
*   words mastered per week
*   sentence pattern mastery
*   review completion rate
*   difficult sound recovery rate

UX KPIs
-------

*   lesson drop-off step
*   replay frequency
*   mic permission acceptance
*   dialogue completion rate

* * *

24\. Sample lesson JSON shape
=============================

```
{
  "lesson_id": "lesson_009",
  "title": "Water and Yes",
  "sound_focus_id": "sound_w",
  "estimated_minutes": 12,
  "words": [
    "word_water",
    "word_we",
    "word_yes",
    "word_you",
    "word_yellow"
  ],
  "sentences": [
    "sentence_i_want_water",
    "sentence_yes_please"
  ],
  "steps": [
    {
      "step_type": "audio_listen",
      "instruction_th": "ฟังเสียง",
      "payload": {
        "sound_id": "sound_w"
      }
    },
    {
      "step_type": "syllable_drill",
      "instruction_th": "พูดตามพยางค์",
      "payload": {
        "syllables": ["wa", "we", "wo"]
      }
    },
    {
      "step_type": "word_flashcard",
      "payload": {
        "word_ids": ["word_water", "word_we", "word_yes"]
      }
    },
    {
      "step_type": "speak_sentence",
      "payload": {
        "sentence_id": "sentence_i_want_water"
      }
    },
    {
      "step_type": "dialogue_turn",
      "payload": {
        "prompt_audio": "asset_prompt_do_you_want_water",
        "valid_answers": ["Yes, please.", "Yes please."]
      }
    }
  ]
}
```

* * *

Frontend

*   Supabase
*   PostgreSQL
*   Storage
*   Edge functions

Option B:

*   Firebase Auth
*   Firestore
*   Cloud Functions
*   Cloud Storage

Speech layer

*   TTS provider
*   STT provider

*   asset uploader

*   CMS
*   analytics

* * *

27\. Final product definition
=============================

This app is not a general English app. It is a **guided spoken-English starter system for Thai beginners**.

Its differentiators are:

*   Thai-first support
*   pronunciation-first design
*   syllable-level teaching
*   small practical daily words
*   beginner-safe voice conversation
*   specific support for Thai learner pronunciation problems

* * *

================================

For the first release, build these first:

1.  Splash
2.  Language select
3.  Onboarding
4.  Home
5.  Lesson player
6.  Word detail
7.  Sound practice
8.  Dialogue practice
9.  Pronunciation feedback
10.  Review screen
11.  Progress screen
12.  Settings
13.  Admin lesson editor
14.  Admin word editor

==============================================

If you want the leanest launch schema, start with:

*   users
*   user\_settings
*   courses
*   levels
*   modules
*   lessons
*   lesson\_steps
*   words
*   sentences
*   sounds
*   dialogues
*   assets
*   lesson\_words
*   lesson\_sentences
*   user\_lesson\_progress
*   user\_word\_progress
*   user\_speaking\_attempts
*   review\_queue

That is enough to ship the first version.
