3\. Firebase core services
--------------------------

3.1 FirebaseAuthService
-----------------------

Responsibilities:

*   anonymous sign-in
*   email sign-in
*   email sign-up
*   sign-out
*   auth state stream
*   current user UID

Example:

```
class FirebaseAuthService {
  final FirebaseAuth _auth;
  FirebaseAuthService(this._auth);

  Stream<User?> authStateChanges() => _auth.authStateChanges();

  User? get currentUser => _auth.currentUser;

  Future<UserCredential> signInAnonymously() {
    return _auth.signInAnonymously();
  }

  Future<UserCredential> signInWithEmail(String email, String password) {
    return _auth.signInWithEmailAndPassword(email: email, password: password);
  }

  Future<UserCredential> signUpWithEmail(String email, String password) {
    return _auth.createUserWithEmailAndPassword(email: email, password: password);
  }

  Future<void> signOut() => _auth.signOut();
}
```

* * *

3.2 FirestoreService
--------------------

Responsibilities:

*   typed access wrappers
*   convenience methods
*   common path builders

Example:

```
class FirestoreService {
  final FirebaseFirestore _db;
  FirestoreService(this._db);

  DocumentReference<Map<String, dynamic>> userDoc(String uid) =>
      _db.collection('users').doc(uid);

  CollectionReference<Map<String, dynamic>> lessonSteps(String lessonId) =>
      _db.collection('lessons').doc(lessonId).collection('steps');

  CollectionReference<Map<String, dynamic>> userLessonProgress(String uid) =>
      _db.collection('users').doc(uid).collection('lessonProgress');

  CollectionReference<Map<String, dynamic>> userReviewQueue(String uid) =>
      _db.collection('users').doc(uid).collection('reviewQueue');
}
```

* * *

3.3 StorageService
------------------

Responsibilities:

*   upload learner recordings
*   resolve download URLs
*   delete learner recordings where needed

Example:

```
class StorageService {
  final FirebaseStorage _storage;
  StorageService(this._storage);

  Future<String> uploadUserRecording({
    required String uid,
    required String localPath,
    required String fileName,
    required DateTime now,
  }) async {
    final ref = _storage.ref().child(
      'user-recordings/users/$uid/${now.year}/${now.month.toString().padLeft(2, '0')}/$fileName',
    );
    await ref.putFile(File(localPath));
    return ref.fullPath;
  }

  Future<String> getDownloadUrl(String storagePath) {
    return _storage.ref(storagePath).getDownloadURL();
  }

  Future<void> delete(String storagePath) {
    return _storage.ref(storagePath).delete();
  }
}
```

* * *

3.4 CloudFunctionsService
-------------------------

Responsibilities:

*   invoke callable functions
*   rebuild derived docs
*   optional server-side actions later

Example:

```
class CloudFunctionsService {
  final FirebaseFunctions _functions;
  CloudFunctionsService(this._functions);

  Future<void> rebuildDerivedHome() async {
    await _functions.httpsCallable('rebuildDerivedHome').call();
  }

  Future<void> rebuildDerivedProgress() async {
    await _functions.httpsCallable('rebuildDerivedProgress').call();
  }
}
```

* * *

4\. Repository pattern for Firebase version
-------------------------------------------

Use this layering:

*   Firebase service
*   datasource
*   repository
*   controller/provider

Example flow
------------

Screen → Controller → Repository → Firebase datasource/service

Never call Firestore directly from widgets.

* * *

5\. Shared domain models
------------------------

Use domain models independent of Firebase document shape.

Examples:

*   `AppUser`
*   `Lesson`
*   `LessonStep`
*   `Word`
*   `Sentence`
*   `Sound`
*   `Dialogue`
*   `ReviewQueueItem`
*   `HomeDashboard`
*   `ProgressDashboard`

Use Freezed for immutable models.

Example:

```
@freezed
class Word with _$Word {
  const factory Word({
    required String id,
    required String englishText,
    required String thaiText,
    String? pronunciationHint,
    String? ipa,
    required List<String> syllableSplit,
    required String category,
    required String audioNormalUrl,
    required String audioSlowUrl,
    String? imageUrl,
  }) = _Word;

  factory Word.fromJson(Map<String, dynamic> json) => _$WordFromJson(json);
}
```

* * *

6\. Auth feature wiring
-----------------------

Repository
----------

```
abstract class AuthRepository {
  Stream<AppUser?> authStateChanges();
  Future<void> signInGuest();
  Future<void> signInEmail(String email, String password);
  Future<void> signUpEmail(String email, String password, String displayName);
  Future<void> signOut();
}
```

Implementation
--------------

*   sign in via Firebase Auth
*   create `users/{uid}` doc if missing
*   create `users/{uid}/settings/default` if missing

Important:  
Guest auth must create a Firestore user document on first sign-in.

* * *

7\. Onboarding feature wiring
-----------------------------

Data locations
--------------

*   `users/{uid}`
*   `users/{uid}/settings/default`
*   `users/{uid}/onboardingSessions/{sessionId}`
*   `users/{uid}/onboardingSessions/{sessionId}/answers/{questionId}`

Repository methods
------------------

```
abstract class OnboardingRepository {
  Future<String> startOnboarding({
    required String interfaceLanguage,
    required String learningGoal,
  });

  Future<void> saveProfile({
    required String sessionId,
    required String displayName,
    required String nativeLanguage,
    required String learningGoal,
    required String pace,
  });

  Future<void> savePlacementAnswer({
    required String sessionId,
    required String questionId,
    required Map<String, dynamic> answer,
  });

  Future<void> completeOnboarding(String sessionId);
}
```

Implementation detail:

*   use generated doc ID for onboarding session
*   write placement answers under subcollection
*   update `users/{uid}` currentLevelId and currentLessonId on completion

* * *

8\. Home feature wiring
-----------------------

Read model
----------

Home screen should read:

*   `users/{uid}`
*   `users/{uid}/derived/home`

Repository
----------

```
abstract class HomeRepository {
  Stream<HomeDashboard> watchHomeDashboard();
  Future<HomeDashboard> getHomeDashboard();
}
```

Implementation
--------------

Use combined reads:

1.  user root doc
2.  derived home doc

Map to `HomeDashboard`.

If derived doc missing:

*   call Cloud Function `rebuildDerivedHome`
*   retry fetch once

* * *

9\. Course feature wiring
-------------------------

Read model
----------

*   `courses/{courseId}`
*   `levels/{levelId}`
*   `modules/{moduleId}`
*   `units/{unitId}`
*   `lessons/{lessonId}`

For mobile MVP:  
Prefer loading the default course map with batched reads.

Repository
----------

```
abstract class CourseRepository {
  Future<CourseMap> getDefaultCourseMap();
}
```

Implementation options:

*   either read direct linked IDs from course/level/module/unit docs
*   or create one denormalized doc later: `appConfig/courseMap/default`

For MVP, linked ID reads are acceptable.

* * *

10\. Lessons feature wiring
---------------------------

This is the most important Firebase integration.

Data locations
--------------

*   `lessons/{lessonId}`
*   `lessons/{lessonId}/steps/*`
*   `users/{uid}/lessonProgress/{lessonId}`
*   `users/{uid}/lessonProgress/{lessonId}/steps/{stepId}`

Repository
----------

```
abstract class LessonRepository {
  Future<Lesson> getLesson(String lessonId);
  Future<List<LessonStep>> getLessonSteps(String lessonId);
  Stream<LessonProgress?> watchLessonProgress(String lessonId);
  Future<void> startLesson(String lessonId);
  Future<void> saveStepProgress({
    required String lessonId,
    required String stepId,
    required Map<String, dynamic> progress,
  });
  Future<void> completeLesson({
    required String lessonId,
    required double overall,
    required double pronunciation,
    required double comprehension,
  });
}
```

Firestore implementation notes
------------------------------

### startLesson

Write:  
`users/{uid}/lessonProgress/{lessonId}`

Example fields:

```
{
  'lessonId': lessonId,
  'status': 'in_progress',
  'startedAt': FieldValue.serverTimestamp(),
  'completedAt': null,
  'completionPercent': 0,
  'currentStepId': '${lessonId}_step_001',
  'retryCount': 0,
  'timeSpentSeconds': 0,
  'scoreOverall': null,
  'pronunciationScore': null,
  'comprehensionScore': null,
  'updatedAt': FieldValue.serverTimestamp(),
}
```

### saveStepProgress

Write:  
`users/{uid}/lessonProgress/{lessonId}/steps/{stepId}`

Also merge update parent lessonProgress doc:

*   currentStepId
*   completionPercent
*   timeSpentSeconds
*   updatedAt

### completeLesson

Update:

*   status = completed
*   completedAt = serverTimestamp
*   final scores

Then optionally call:

*   `rebuildDerivedHome`
*   `rebuildDerivedProgress`

* * *

Session ID
----------

15\. Review feature wiring
--------------------------

Data locations
--------------

*   `users/{uid}/reviewQueue/*`

Repository
----------

```
abstract class ReviewRepository {
  Stream<List<ReviewQueueItem>> watchDueReviewQueue();
  Future<List<ReviewQueueItem>> getDueReviewQueue();
  Future<void> completeReviewItem({
    required String reviewId,
    required String result,
    required String confidence,
    required int timeSpentSeconds,
    double? score,
  });
}
```

Implementation
--------------

Read:

```
db
 .collection('users')
 .doc(uid)
 .collection('reviewQueue')
 .where('dueAt', isLessThanOrEqualTo: Timestamp.now())
 .orderBy('dueAt')
```

When completed:

*   update `completedAt`
*   optionally reduce priority or delete item after completion depending on review policy

For MVP:  
mark `completedAt`.

18\. Downloads wiring
---------------------

--------------

*   `users/{uid}/downloads/{packId}`

Repository
----------

```
abstract class DownloadsRepository {
  Future<List<DownloadPack>> listPacks();
  Future<void> markDownloaded(String packId, int version);
  Future<void> removeDownloaded(String packId);
}
```

Actual file download can remain local-only.  
Firestore can store only download state summary.

* * *

19\. Speaking pipeline wiring
-----------------------------

Services involved
-----------------

*   `AudioRecordService`
*   `StorageService`
*   optional speech scoring API service

Because Firebase itself does not transcribe/score audio by default, you have two practical options:

### Option A

Use your own speech backend/API alongside Firebase.

### Option B

Call a Cloud Function that forwards audio to speech services.

For this project, keep the abstraction:

```
abstract class SpeechRepository {
  Future<SpeechUploadResult> uploadRecording(String localPath);
  Future<TranscriptResult> transcribe({
    required String storagePath,
    required Map<String, dynamic> context,
  });
  Future<PronunciationResult> scoreWord({
    required String storagePath,
    required String wordId,
    required String targetText,
  });
  Future<PronunciationResult> scoreSentence({
    required String storagePath,
    required String sentenceId,
    required String targetText,
  });
  Future<PronunciationResult> scoreSound({
    required String storagePath,
    required String soundId,
  });
  Future<void> saveAttempt(SpeakingAttemptInput input);
}
```

This repository may hit:

*   Firebase Storage for upload
*   Cloud Functions or external API for scoring
*   Firestore for attempt persistence

* * *

20\. Riverpod provider layout
-----------------------------

Firebase core providers
-----------------------

```
final firebaseAuthProvider = Provider<FirebaseAuth>((ref) => FirebaseAuth.instance);
final firestoreProvider = Provider<FirebaseFirestore>((ref) => FirebaseFirestore.instance);
final firebaseStorageProvider = Provider<FirebaseStorage>((ref) => FirebaseStorage.instance);
final firebaseFunctionsProvider = Provider<FirebaseFunctions>((ref) => FirebaseFunctions.instance);

final firebaseAuthServiceProvider = Provider(
  (ref) => FirebaseAuthService(ref.read(firebaseAuthProvider)),
);

final firestoreServiceProvider = Provider(
  (ref) => FirestoreService(ref.read(firestoreProvider)),
);

final storageServiceProvider = Provider(
  (ref) => StorageService(ref.read(firebaseStorageProvider)),
);

final cloudFunctionsServiceProvider = Provider(
  (ref) => CloudFunctionsService(ref.read(firebaseFunctionsProvider)),
);
```

Repository providers
--------------------

```
final authRepositoryProvider = Provider<AuthRepository>((ref) {
  return FirebaseAuthRepository(
    ref.read(firebaseAuthServiceProvider),
    ref.read(firestoreServiceProvider),
  );
});

final lessonRepositoryProvider = Provider<LessonRepository>((ref) {
  return FirestoreLessonRepository(
    ref.read(firestoreServiceProvider),
    ref.read(cloudFunctionsServiceProvider),
  );
});
```

* * *

21\. Example repository implementation: Firestore lesson repository
-------------------------------------------------------------------

```
class FirestoreLessonRepository implements LessonRepository {
  final FirestoreService _firestore;
  final CloudFunctionsService _functions;

  FirestoreLessonRepository(this._firestore, this._functions);

  @override
  Future<Lesson> getLesson(String lessonId) async {
    final snap = await FirebaseFirestore.instance.collection('lessons').doc(lessonId).get();
    if (!snap.exists) throw Exception('Lesson not found');
    return Lesson.fromJson(snap.data()!..['id'] = snap.id);
  }

  @override
  Future<List<LessonStep>> getLessonSteps(String lessonId) async {
    final snap = await FirebaseFirestore.instance
        .collection('lessons')
        .doc(lessonId)
        .collection('steps')
        .orderBy('stepOrder')
        .get();

    return snap.docs
        .map((d) => LessonStep.fromJson(d.data()..['id'] = d.id))
        .toList();
  }

  @override
  Future<void> startLesson(String lessonId) async {
    final uid = FirebaseAuth.instance.currentUser!.uid;
    await FirebaseFirestore.instance
        .collection('users')
        .doc(uid)
        .collection('lessonProgress')
        .doc(lessonId)
        .set({
      'lessonId': lessonId,
      'status': 'in_progress',
      'startedAt': FieldValue.serverTimestamp(),
      'completedAt': null,
      'completionPercent': 0,
      'currentStepId': '${lessonId}_step_001',
      'retryCount': 0,
      'timeSpentSeconds': 0,
      'scoreOverall': null,
      'pronunciationScore': null,
      'comprehensionScore': null,
      'updatedAt': FieldValue.serverTimestamp(),
    }, SetOptions(merge: true));
  }

  @override
  Stream<LessonProgress?> watchLessonProgress(String lessonId) {
    final uid = FirebaseAuth.instance.currentUser!.uid;
    return FirebaseFirestore.instance
        .collection('users')
        .doc(uid)
        .collection('lessonProgress')
        .doc(lessonId)
        .snapshots()
        .map((snap) => snap.exists ? LessonProgress.fromJson(snap.data()!) : null);
  }

  @override
  Future<void> saveStepProgress({
    required String lessonId,
    required String stepId,
    required Map<String, dynamic> progress,
  }) async {
    final uid = FirebaseAuth.instance.currentUser!.uid;

    await FirebaseFirestore.instance
        .collection('users')
        .doc(uid)
        .collection('lessonProgress')
        .doc(lessonId)
        .collection('steps')
        .doc(stepId)
        .set({
      ...progress,
      'stepId': stepId,
      'updatedAt': FieldValue.serverTimestamp(),
    }, SetOptions(merge: true));
  }

  @override
  Future<void> completeLesson({
    required String lessonId,
    required double overall,
    required double pronunciation,
    required double comprehension,
  }) async {
    final uid = FirebaseAuth.instance.currentUser!.uid;

    await FirebaseFirestore.instance
        .collection('users')
        .doc(uid)
        .collection('lessonProgress')
        .doc(lessonId)
        .set({
      'lessonId': lessonId,
      'status': 'completed',
      'completedAt': FieldValue.serverTimestamp(),
      'scoreOverall': overall,
      'pronunciationScore': pronunciation,
      'comprehensionScore': comprehension,
      'completionPercent': 100,
      'updatedAt': FieldValue.serverTimestamp(),
    }, SetOptions(merge: true));

    await _functions.rebuildDerivedHome();
    await _functions.rebuildDerivedProgress();
  }
}
```

* * *

22\. Controllers to build first
-------------------------------

Build these first for Firebase version:

*   `SessionController`
*   `HomeController`
*   `LessonPlayerController`
*   `ReviewSessionController`
*   `DialogueSessionController`
*   `SettingsController`

* * *

23\. Recommended first vertical slice
-------------------------------------

Using Firebase backend, build this order:

1.  Firebase bootstrap
2.  anonymous auth
3.  create `users/{uid}` document
4.  home derived fetch
5.  lesson detail fetch
6.  lesson step fetch
7.  lesson progress write
8.  sentence speaking upload/save attempt
9.  lesson completion
10.  derived home refresh

That is enough to prove the whole stack.

* * *

24\. Firebase-specific cautions
-------------------------------

### Firestore document size

Do not embed large step content arrays inside lesson doc if they grow.  
Keep steps in subcollection.

### Derived docs

Treat derived docs as cache/read models.  
Do not let client own their contents.

### Storage paths

Only store Storage path in learner attempts if you can resolve URL later.  
Do not duplicate very long signed URLs in Firestore.

### Offline sync

Firestore offline mode is useful, but for progress writes with derived docs:

*   be careful with stale UI assumptions
*   prefer showing optimistic local state while server catches up

* * *

------------------------------

The strongest immediate next artifact is a **Flutter project skeleton with Firebase-wired repository interfaces and starter implementations**.

Goal
----

Provide a production-ready checklist for standing up either backend path:

*   **Firebase / Firestore**
*   **Supabase / Postgres**

This checklist is organized by:

1.  environment setup
2.  secrets/config
3.  database
4.  storage
5.  auth
6.  backend functions
7.  mobile app integration
8.  QA and release checks

1\. Environment strategy
========================

Use at least 3 environments:

*   **local**
*   **staging**
*   **production**

Recommended names:

Firebase
--------

*   project: `easy-english-thai-dev`
*   project: `easy-english-thai-staging`
*   project: `easy-english-thai-prod`

Supabase
--------

*   project: `easy-english-thai-dev`
*   project: `easy-english-thai-staging`
*   project: `easy-english-thai-prod`

2\. Shared deployment checklist
===============================

These apply to either backend choice.

2.1 Product configuration
-------------------------

*   confirm primary locale support:
    *   Thai
    *   English
    *   bilingual
*   confirm audio asset naming conventions
*   confirm lesson/content versioning rule
*   confirm production domain names
*   confirm retention policy for learner recordings
*   confirm push notification sender settings

*   admin emails
*   admin auth rules
*   CMS access list

3.1 Create Firebase projects

3.2 Enable services

*   Authentication

*   Storage

*   Anonymous

*   Google
*   Apple

3.5 Deploy Storage rules

3.6 Create Storage structure

*   verify dialogues and turns created

*   `rebuildDerivedHome`

*   reminder scheduler
*   cleanup scheduler

3.9 Set admin access
--------------------

Create admin user docs with:

```
{
  "role": "admin"
}
```

Prefer adding custom claims too if using Storage admin rules.

3.10 Create indexes
-------------------

Add Firestore indexes for:

*   lessons by `isPublished`, `weekNumber`
*   words by `category`, `difficultyLevel`
*   dialogues by `contextType`, `isPublished`
*   user review queue by `dueAt`

*   test Android token registration
*   test iOS token registration
*   send test review reminder

3.12 App configuration
----------------------

In Flutter:

*   add Firebase options per environment
*   separate bundle IDs/application IDs if needed
*   verify auth, firestore, storage, functions targets per env

3.13 Firebase production checks
-------------------------------

*   no dev project IDs in prod app
*   no open write rules

*   reminder schedules verified
*   seed content published only where intended

4.12 Supabase production checks

10\. Practical recommendation
=============================

If you want the fastest MVP:

*   choose **Firebase** for mobile velocity

If you want the cleaner long-term backend and reporting model:

*   choose **Supabase/Postgres**

Do not try to launch both in production at once.  
Use one as the primary implementation target.

# 8. Acceptance test scenarios for MVP signoff

## Scenario 1 — brand new learner
- installs app
- enters as guest
- selects Thai UI
- completes onboarding
- starts first lesson
- listens, records, retries, completes lesson
- returns to home and sees updated progress

## Scenario 2 — speaking step failure recovery
- learner denies mic permission
- app shows fallback/recovery path
- learner enables permission
- learner records successfully
- transcription/pronunciation feedback shown

## Scenario 3 — review generation
- learner completes lesson
- review items appear later/in due queue
- learner completes review session
- counts update correctly

## Scenario 4 — returning user
- closes app mid-lesson
- reopens app
- resumes from saved step

## Scenario 5 — reminder
- learner sets reminder
- device token registered
- scheduled reminder can be received in test environment

Use this format for actual tracking.

## Title
`[EPIC CODE] Short action-oriented task name`

## Description
- purpose
- scope
- implementation notes
- out of scope

## Acceptance criteria
- bullet list
- test conditions
- error states if relevant

- blocking tasks
- required backend/content readiness

## Labels
- feature area
- platform
- priority
- env

# 10. Example task written in ticket form

## [F3] Implement lesson player controller

### Description
Create the controller that manages lesson session state, current step index, step transitions, progress persistence hooks, and completion routing.

### Acceptance criteria
- loads lesson steps in order
- exposes current step to UI
- supports continue/advance logic
- updates completion percent
- restores current step from saved lesson progress
- emits completed state on final step

### Dependencies
- D2 lesson detail and steps retrieval
- H1 lesson progress model
- F2 step renderer framework

### Owner
FE

### Priority
P0

---

# 11. Best immediate execution order

If you want the fastest real build, start implementation in this order:

1. foundation setup  
2. guest auth  
3. onboarding  
4. home dashboard  
5. lesson detail + steps  
6. lesson player controller  
7. audio playback  
8. mic + recording  
9. progress persistence  
10. lesson completion  
11. review queue  
12. settings + reminders  
13. dialogues  
14. admin cleanup and QA

That gives a usable pilot faster than trying to build everything evenly.

from pathlib import Path

content = r"""# Easy English Thai — Admin CMS specification

## Purpose
This document defines the standalone **Admin CMS** for managing the English-learning app content.

It covers:
- admin roles and permissions
- information architecture
- screen inventory
- workflows
- content models
- validation rules
- publishing lifecycle
- QA tooling
- operational requirements

This spec is aligned with the previously defined:
- API contract
- OpenAPI spec
- Supabase/Postgres schema
- Firebase/Firestore schema
- Flutter/mobile product structure

---

# 1. CMS goals

The CMS exists to let authorized staff:

- create and edit curriculum structure
- manage lessons, sounds, words, sentences, dialogues, and packs
- upload and attach media assets
- publish or unpublish content safely
- detect content gaps before release
- review basic learner-impacting metrics

The CMS is **not** intended for:
- full BI/warehouse analytics
- support ticketing
- subscription/billing operations
- freeform AI content generation in MVP

---

# 2. Primary admin users

## 2.1 Content manager
Responsibilities:
- create/edit lessons
- manage word/sentence/sound/dialogue content
- manage publishing

## 2.2 Linguistic reviewer
Responsibilities:
- verify Thai meanings
- verify pronunciation hints
- verify sentence naturalness
- verify dialogue correctness

## 2.3 Audio/media editor
Responsibilities:
- upload audio/image assets
- attach assets to content
- replace broken media
- confirm format/duration quality

## 2.4 QA/content operations
Responsibilities:
- run QA reports
- find missing content
- verify lesson completeness
- support release checklist

## 2.5 Admin/super admin
Responsibilities:
- role assignment
- content publishing authority
- system configuration
- audit access

---

# 3. Role and permission model

## Roles
- `content_editor`
- `linguistic_reviewer`
- `media_editor`
- `qa_editor`
- `admin`
- `super_admin`

## Permission groups

### Content structure
- view courses
- edit courses
- edit levels/modules/units
- reorder lessons

### Lesson content
- create lesson
- edit lesson
- add/edit steps
- publish lesson

### Library content
- create/edit words
- create/edit sentences
- create/edit sounds
- create/edit minimal pairs
- create/edit dialogues

### Media
- upload asset
- replace asset
- delete asset
- attach asset to content

### QA
- view QA reports
- resolve QA issues
- export QA list

### Admin
- manage users/roles
- view audit log
- publish global content
- change config

## Recommended permissions by role

### content_editor
- content structure: yes
- lesson content: yes
- library content: yes
- media upload: no
- QA: limited
- admin: no

### linguistic_reviewer
- content structure: read
- lesson content: edit text only
- library content: edit text only
- media: no
- QA: yes
- admin: no

### media_editor
- content structure: read
- lesson content: limited
- library content: limited
- media: yes
- QA: limited
- admin: no

### qa_editor
- view all content
- view QA reports
- mark issues resolved
- no publish unless explicitly granted

### admin
- all standard content and publish permissions

### super_admin
- all permissions including role management and system settings

---

## Main navigation
- Dashboard
- Curriculum
- Lessons
- Words
- Sentences
- Sounds
- Dialogues
- Minimal Pairs
- Assets

- QA Reports

For MVP, the minimum practical nav is:
- Dashboard
- Curriculum
- Lessons
- Words
- Sentences
- Sounds
- Dialogues
- Assets
- QA Reports

  - upload asset

- open QA issue list
- open recent content edits

## Data requirements
- lesson counts by publish state
- issue counts by type
- recent content activity
- optional learner trend summary

# 7. Lesson management specification

## 7.1 Lesson list screen
Filters:
- unit
- week/module
- level
- published/draft
- sound focus
- search text

Columns:
- lesson ID
- title
- subtitle
- lesson type
- sound focus
- estimated minutes
- step count
- publish state
- last updated

Bulk actions:
- publish
- unpublish
- export
- move unit optional

## 7.2 Lesson detail/editor screen

### Header
- lesson ID
- title
- subtitle
- publish badge
- save button
- publish/unpublish button
- preview button

### Metadata section
Fields:
- unit
- lesson order
- title
- subtitle
- estimated minutes
- lesson type
- sound focus
- review lesson flag

### Targets section
- target words
- target sentences

Actions:
- add/remove word
- add/remove sentence
- reorder targets optional

### Steps section
Displays ordered lesson steps.

Each step row shows:
- step order
- step type
- instruction EN
- instruction TH
- payload summary
- passing rule summary

Actions:
- add step
- edit step
- duplicate step
- delete step
- drag reorder

### Validation panel
Checks:
- has title
- has at least one step
- steps in valid order
- required targets exist
- referenced assets exist
- no broken sound/word/sentence references

## 7.3 Step editor modal/screen
Fields:
- step type
- step order
- instruction EN
- instruction TH
- payload JSON or structured fields
- passing rule JSON or structured fields

Structured step forms should exist for common step types.

### audio_listen
Fields:
- sound ID or asset
- autoplay optional
- slow version optional

### syllable_drill
Fields:
- syllables list
- prompt text
- target sound

### word_flashcard
Fields:
- selected word IDs
- reveal mode
- audio enabled

### speak_sentence
Fields:
- target sentence ID
- minimum attempts
- scoring enabled

### dialogue_turn
Fields:
- dialogue ID or inline prompt reference
- hint mode
- retry limit

# 16. QA reports specification

## Goal
Catch publish-blocking content issues early.

## Report types
- missing normal audio
- missing slow audio
- missing image
- missing Thai translation
- missing pronunciation hint
- missing target words in lesson
- missing lesson steps
- broken asset references
- empty dialogue expected answers
- missing sentence pattern
- unused assets
- unpublished content referenced by published lesson/dialogue

## QA report screen
Filters:
- issue type
- content type
- severity
- open/resolved
- published only

Columns:
- issue ID
- content type
- content ID
- issue type
- severity
- status
- created at

Actions:
- open content
- mark resolved
- export CSV
- batch resolve optional

## Severity model
- blocker
- high
- medium
- low

### Blocker examples
- published lesson with no steps
- published lesson references missing content
- dialogue with invalid turn order
- required audio missing for mandatory speaking/listening flow

---

# 20. Audit log specification

Track who changed what.

## Audit log entries
- actor
- timestamp
- entity type
- entity ID
- action
- before/after summary optional

Tracked actions:
- create
- update
- delete
- publish
- unpublish
- role change
- asset replace

## Audit log screen
Filters:
- actor
- action
- entity type
- date range

---

# 21. Publishing lifecycle

## States
- draft
- ready_for_review optional
- published
- unpublished

For MVP, minimum states can be:
- draft
- published

## Publish rules
A lesson can be published only if:
- required metadata complete
- at least one step exists
- referenced words/sentences/sounds exist
- required assets exist
- no blocker QA issues

A dialogue can be published only if:
- title/description/context/mode/level present
- at least one turn exists
- turn ordering valid
- learner turns with validation need expected answers

## Unpublish rules
Unpublishing is allowed for admins.
Warn if currently referenced from published parent structures.

---

# 22. Validation rules by content type

## Lessons
- title required
- unit required
- lesson order required
- estimated minutes > 0
- lesson type valid
- step count > 0 before publish

## Steps
- step order unique within lesson
- valid step type
- instruction EN/TH required
- payload shape valid for chosen type

## Words
- English required
- Thai required
- category required
- difficulty valid
- syllable split non-empty

## Sentences
- English required
- Thai required
- valid sentence pattern
- target words should exist

## Sounds
- code unique
- display symbol required
- category required

## Dialogues
- title required
- mode valid
- level required
- turn order unique
- learner expected answers required for validated turns

## Assets
- supported MIME type
- file path/url valid
- metadata shape valid for asset type

---

# 23. CMS workflow details

## Workflow A — create a new lesson
1. Open Lessons
2. Click Create Lesson
3. Enter metadata
4. Save draft
5. Add target words and sentences
6. Add steps
7. Run validation
8. Fix issues
9. Publish

## Workflow B — replace broken audio
1. Open QA report
2. Filter missing/broken audio
3. Open asset/content detail
4. Upload replacement
5. Attach replacement asset
6. Re-run validation
7. Mark issue resolved

## Workflow C — add new dialogue
1. Open Dialogues
2. Create metadata
3. Add target phrases
4. Add turns
5. Add hints and expected answers
6. Validate
7. Publish

## Workflow D — reorder lessons inside week
1. Open Curriculum > unit
2. Drag lesson rows
3. Save order
4. Validate no duplicate order numbers
5. Republish or auto-apply order

---

# 24. API dependencies for CMS

The CMS depends on admin endpoints already defined, including:
- `/admin/lessons`
- `/admin/lessons/{lesson_id}`
- `/admin/lessons/{lesson_id}/steps`
- `/admin/lessons/{lesson_id}/steps/reorder`
- `/admin/lessons/{lesson_id}/publish`
- `/admin/words`
- `/admin/words/{word_id}`
- `/admin/sentences`
- `/admin/sounds`
- `/admin/dialogues`
- `/admin/dialogues/{dialogue_id}/turns`
- `/admin/assets`
- `/admin/content-qa`
- `/admin/analytics/summary`

If Firebase is used directly instead of a custom admin API, equivalent admin services must be created in Cloud Functions or trusted web backend logic.

---

# 25. Recommended frontend architecture for CMS

## Stack
Best practical options:
- React + TypeScript + Next.js
- React Query
- component library such as MUI
- form library such as React Hook Form + Zod

## Pages
- dashboard
- lessons list/detail
- words list/detail
- sentences list/detail
- sounds list/detail
- dialogues list/detail
- asset library
- QA reports

## State model
- server state with React Query
- form state with RHF
- optimistic updates only where safe
- publishing actions should confirm and refetch

---

# 26. CMS non-functional requirements

## Performance
- list screens load in under 2 seconds for normal dataset sizes
- editor screens load in under 3 seconds
- search/filter responsive

## Reliability
- autosave optional later
- explicit save in MVP
- prevent silent data loss on navigation away

## Security
- admin-only access
- role-based action gating
- audit critical changes
- private assets and secrets protected

## Accessibility
- keyboard navigation for editors
- visible labels
- color contrast acceptable
- form validation readable

---

# 27. MVP CMS cut

To launch MVP, the minimum admin CMS must include:

- login/admin auth
- dashboard basic
- lesson list/detail/editor
- step editor
- word list/detail/editor
- sentence list/detail/editor
- sound list/detail/editor
- dialogue list/detail/editor
- asset upload/library
- publish/unpublish
- QA report for missing audio and broken references

Everything else can follow later.

---

# 28. Recommended implementation backlog for CMS

## Phase 1
- admin auth
- dashboard basic
- lesson list/detail
- word list/detail
- asset upload

## Phase 2
- sentence editor
- sound editor
- publish workflow
- QA report basic

## Phase 3
- dialogue editor
- curriculum reorder
- analytics summary
- audit log

---

# 29. Acceptance criteria for CMS MVP

The CMS MVP is ready when:
- an admin can create/edit/publish a lesson without DB manual edits
- an admin can attach words, sentences, and sounds to lessons
- an admin can upload and attach audio assets
- a QA user can detect missing audio and broken references
- a dialogue can be created and published
- learner app reads updated published content correctly

---

- a **CMS wireframe spec**
- a **React/Next.js admin frontend architecture**
- a **CMS implementation backlog with tickets**
- a **Zod/JSON schema validation pack for admin forms**

# 10. Recommended decision points

## Decision 1 — backend choice
Choose one:
- Firebase for speed
- Supabase for long-term relational clarity

Do not build both as live production backends at the same time.

## Decision 2 — speech scoring architecture
Choose one:
- external speech API behind backend/functions
- direct speech microservice
- Cloud Function proxy

## Decision 3 — admin tooling
Choose one:
- basic CMS for MVP
- manual seed + light admin operations first
- fuller CMS after pilot

---

# 11. Best practical implementation order

## Option A — fastest MVP path
1. Firebase rules and seed
2. Firebase functions starter
3. Flutter Firebase repository layer
4. MVP backlog execution
5. deployment checklist
6. admin CMS after pilot stabilization

## Option B — long-term backend path
1. Supabase schema
2. RLS policies
3. storage policies
4. seed data
5. custom backend from OpenAPI
6. Flutter app against API
7. admin CMS

---
